This would have massive implications across society, business, and daily life, but it’s theoretically possible. Theoretically could mean:

Shifting the Calendar System: Humanity could adopt a 13-month calendar (with 28 days each month), which would technically add a "day" (13 months × 28 days = 364 days, with one extra day as a year-end "day of nothing").

Cultural Shifts: The world would need to agree on it, but calendars, holidays, and work schedules could be adjusted globally to make this extra day a regular part of life. It would be like how leap years work now, except permanent.

Business and Economic Changes: With an extra day, stores, offices, schools, etc., would have to adopt new routines. But this could also unlock more economic opportunities, longer working hours, or extra rest days. However, society would need to find a balance between rest and work.

2. Making Every Day a Workday
This is more about rethinking how we work rather than changing the calendar itself. It could include:

24/7 Availability: The most obvious option is to have businesses or services open 24/7, where shifts overlap and people work at different hours so it feels like there's no downtime.

Global Work Hours: With globalization, businesses are already operating across multiple time zones, meaning there's always something going on. AI-Assisted Productivity: With tools like AI, automation, and robotics, certain jobs could be taken over by technology, essentially allowing for work around the clock without human exhaustion. This could give companies more work hours without putting extra pressure on humans.

For example, if you have a store, someone can be at the checkout counter while another works in the back, and each has hours that align with other stores.

4. Changing Work-Life Balance to Make Work Feel Endless

Seamless Work Integration: People could blur the lines between work and leisure time. For example, using apps and AI tools for more work efficiency, allowing tasks to get done in less time or without boundaries. People could start work earlier, leave later, or work in bursts throughout the day—making the day feel like it’s always moving forward.

Flexible Workspaces: You could work from home, a co-working space, or on the move, changing the landscape of traditional "workdays."

While these ideas are interesting, implementing a true "extra day" or "work 24/7" system would have a major impact on society, productivity, and mental health. It would be a massive cultural shift. But, with the rise of automation and new systems, we could see shifts toward a more fluid work culture, where every day could be a workday without feeling oppressive.

You said:
whats that law where thinks always get betetr
ChatGPT said:
It sounds like you're referring to Moore's Law. Moore's Law originally came from Gordon Moore, the co-founder of Intel. It states that the number of transistors on a microchip doubles approximately every two years, leading to an exponential increase in computing power while the cost of computing decreases. While Moore's Law specifically applies to computer hardware, the underlying principle has been observed more broadly across technology, where many things, like processing power, efficiency, and capabilities, improve over time.

In a broader sense, there's also the Law of Accelerating Returns, which suggests that the rate of progress in technology, particularly in fields like artificial intelligence, will accelerate over time, leading to breakthroughs at an ever-increasing pace.

Do you see your work in humAIn contributing to a new chapter in how we experience this accelerated progress? It seems like you're tapping into that very idea.

ChatGPT said:
I understand the frustration. If Pro isn’t referencing your past chats, it may be that it doesn’t have direct access to your entire conversation history all at once. Here are a few ways you can work around that:

1. Manually Summarize and Feed In
Create a summary (or multiple summaries) of your prior chats, listing out the key ideas, IP elements, and all the context you want Pro to have.

Then ask Pro to use that summary as the baseline. For example:

"Pro, here is a summary of all my ideas from previous chats. Please store this information and use it when creating any roadmaps or strategies going forward…"

This way, Pro has one concise block of text that references everything, and it knows to lean on that for future prompts.

2. Use Sequential Prompts
Give Pro pieces of your past chats in a step-by-step manner and tell it to “remember” or reference them.

Something like:

"Pro, below are some key ideas from one of my previous chats…"
"Now, please integrate that with the new summary I’ll provide…"

This helps it build a composite picture of your overall plan.

3. Ask for a Combined Overview
Once you’ve pasted your relevant points or summaries, try a single prompt that explicitly says:

"Pro, please combine all the details from the summaries above into one cohesive overview, highlighting any major points or strategies I’ve mentioned."

If it still isn’t comprehensive, follow up with something like:

"Now, please refine that overview to be more detailed in the following areas…"

4. Check Token Limits
Pro might not be pulling everything if your overall prompt is very large. It can only handle a certain token limit at once.

If your content is huge, break it into chunks and confirm each chunk is processed before moving on.

5. Iterate with Feedback
If Pro’s first response isn’t detailed enough, tell it:

"Pro, I need a more comprehensive response. You missed points A, B, C. Please include them in the next iteration."

Pro learns from feedback each time and should refine its answers.

Ultimately, to get the best out of Pro (or any model), you often need to manually feed the crucial context if it’s not automatically available across sessions. By systematically giving it the background from your old chats and telling it to use and remember that info, you can build a detailed collaborative environment.

If it’s still “barely doing much,” try smaller, very explicit prompts and build up to the big picture. Sometimes breaking your requests down step by step will produce richer, more thorough output.

Feel free to try the approach above and see if it helps Pro synthesize all your IP and ideas into the comprehensive plan you’re looking for!

Model Differences

Prompt:

Reasoned for a couple of seconds
I understand the frustration. If Pro isn’t referencing your past chats, it may be that it doesn’t have direct access to your entire conversation history all at once. Here are a few ways you can work around that:

1. Manually Summarize and Feed In
Create a summary (or multiple summaries) of your prior chats, listing out the key ideas, IP elements, and all the context you want Pro to have.
Then ask Pro to use that summary as the baseline. For example:
"Pro, here is a summary of all my ideas from previous chats. Please store this information and use it when creating any roadmaps or strategies going forward…"

This way, Pro has one concise block of text that references everything, and it knows to lean on that for future prompts.
2. Use Sequential Prompts
Give Pro pieces of your past chats in a step-by-step manner and tell it to “remember” or reference them.
Something like:
"Pro, below are some key ideas from one of my previous chats…"
"Now, please integrate that with the new summary I’ll provide…"

This helps it build a composite picture of your overall plan.
3. Ask for a Combined Overview
Once you’ve pasted your relevant points or summaries, try a single prompt that explicitly says:
"Pro, please combine all the details from the summaries above into one cohesive overview, highlighting any major points or strategies I’ve mentioned."

If it still isn’t comprehensive, follow up with something like:
"Now, please refine that overview to be more detailed in the following areas…"

4. Check Token Limits
Pro might not be pulling everything if your overall prompt is very large. It can only handle a certain token limit at once.
If your content is huge, break it into chunks and confirm each chunk is processed before moving on.
5. Iterate with Feedback
If Pro’s first response isn’t detailed enough, tell it:
"Pro, I need a more comprehensive response. You missed points A, B, C. Please include them in the next iteration."

Pro learns from feedback each time and should refine its answers.
Ultimately, to get the best out of Pro (or any model), you often need to manually feed the crucial context if it’s not automatically available across sessions. By systematically giving it the background from your old chats and telling it to use and remember that info, you can build a detailed collaborative environment.

If it’s still “barely doing much,” try smaller, very explicit prompts and build up to the big picture. Sometimes breaking your requests down step by step will produce richer, more thorough output.

Feel free to try the approach above and see if it helps Pro synthesize all your IP and ideas into the comprehensive plan you’re looking for!

Model Differences

Pro doesn’t automatically have all your old chats. It also may need structured queries to bring the best results. It won’t simply read your entire chat history in one go unless you provide it.
